\Hypertarget{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_ad954823b5135fdbb850d488ba11aaf6f}\index{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}!add\_condition@{add\_condition}}
\index{add\_condition@{add\_condition}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{add\_condition()}{add\_condition()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_ad954823b5135fdbb850d488ba11aaf6f} 
 "{}Parser\+Element"{} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+add\+\_\+condition (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacesetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_ad113bb1ecfec492f399f88aecf5df735}{Parse\+Condition}}}]{fns}{, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{kwargs}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Add a boolean predicate function to expression's list of parse actions. See
:class:`set_parse_action` for function call signatures. Unlike ``set_parse_action``,
functions passed to ``add_condition`` need to return boolean success/fail of the condition.

Optional keyword arguments:

- message = define a custom message to be used in the raised exception
- fatal = if True, will raise ParseFatalException to stop parsing immediately; otherwise will raise
  ParseException
- call_during_try = boolean to indicate if this method should be called during internal tryParse calls,
  default=False

Example::

    integer = Word(nums).set_parse_action(lambda toks: int(toks[0]))
    year_int = integer.copy()
    year_int.add_condition(lambda toks: toks[0] >= 2000, message="Only support years 2000 and later")
    date_str = year_int + '/' + integer + '/' + integer

    result = date_str.parse_string("1999/12/31")  # -> Exception: Only support years 2000 and later (at char 0),
                                                                 (line:1, col:1)
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definición en la línea \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2setuptools_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source_l00693}{693}} del archivo \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2setuptools_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source}{core.\+py}}.

\index{copy@{copy}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{copy()}{copy()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a8fe5f362502288698dd516b7fa6d88e6} 
 "{}Parser\+Element"{} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+copy (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Make a copy of this :class:`ParserElement`.  Useful for defining
different parse actions for the same parsing pattern, using copies of
the original parse element.

Example::

    integer = Word(nums).set_parse_action(lambda toks: int(toks[0]))
    integerK = integer.copy().add_parse_action(lambda toks: toks[0] * 1024) + Suppress("K")
    integerM = integer.copy().add_parse_action(lambda toks: toks[0] * 1024 * 1024) + Suppress("M")

    print((integerK | integerM | integer)[1, ...].parse_string("5K 100 640K 256M"))

prints::

    [5120, 100, 655360, 268435456]

Equivalent form of ``expr.copy()`` is just ``expr()``::

    integerM = integer().add_parse_action(lambda toks: toks[0] * 1024 * 1024) + Suppress("M")
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplementado en \mbox{\hyperlink{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_forward_a92cd3aadd8cbdba01f2cdccad1e6fa4e}{setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Forward}} y \mbox{\hyperlink{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parse_expression_ae88ccf3b2fcd7cde4dcd6cfbb93a4c0a}{setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parse\+Expression}}.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_ab7e3f532f6e7783243272292e1f604b3} 
 None setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+create\+\_\+diagram (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{Union\mbox{[}Text\+IO, Path, str\mbox{]}}]{output\+\_\+html}{, }\item[{int }]{vertical}{ = {\ttfamily 3}, }\item[{bool }]{show\+\_\+results\+\_\+names}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{bool }]{show\+\_\+groups}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{kwargs}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Create a railroad diagram for the parser.

Parameters:
- output_html (str or file-like object) - output target for generated
  diagram HTML
- vertical (int) - threshold for formatting multiple alternatives vertically
  instead of horizontally (default=3)
- show_results_names - bool flag whether diagram should show annotations for
  defined results names
- show_groups - bool flag whether groups should be highlighted with an unlabeled surrounding box
Additional diagram-formatting keyword arguments can also be included;
see railroad.Diagram class.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a5cc9ff3d61633b302af203694626aaec}\index{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}!disable\_memoization@{disable\_memoization}}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a5cc9ff3d61633b302af203694626aaec} 
 None setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+disable\+\_\+memoization (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Disables active Packrat or Left Recursion parsing and their memoization

This method also works if neither Packrat nor Left Recursion are enabled.
This makes it safe to call before activating Packrat nor Left Recursion
to clear any previous settings.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a6b306193a89efafdcf1592bc73d1a392}\index{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}!enable\_left\_recursion@{enable\_left\_recursion}}
\index{enable\_left\_recursion@{enable\_left\_recursion}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{enable\_left\_recursion()}{enable\_left\_recursion()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a6b306193a89efafdcf1592bc73d1a392} 
 None setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+enable\+\_\+left\+\_\+recursion (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{typing.\+Optional\mbox{[}int\mbox{]} }]{cache\+\_\+size\+\_\+limit}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{}]{force}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Enables "bounded recursion" parsing, which allows for both direct and indirect
left-recursion. During parsing, left-recursive :class:`Forward` elements are
repeatedly matched with a fixed recursion depth that is gradually increased
until finding the longest match.

Example::

    import pyparsing as pp
    pp.ParserElement.enable_left_recursion()

    E = pp.Forward("E")
    num = pp.Word(pp.nums)
    # match `num`, or `num '+' num`, or `num '+' num '+' num`, ...
    E <<= E + '+' - num | num

    print(E.parse_string("1+2+3"))

Recursion search naturally memoizes matches of ``Forward`` elements and may
thus skip reevaluation of parse actions during backtracking. This may break
programs with parse actions which rely on strict ordering of side-effects.

Parameters:

- cache_size_limit - (default=``None``) - memoize at most this many
  ``Forward`` elements during matching; if ``None`` (the default),
  memoize all ``Forward`` elements.

Bounded Recursion parsing works similar but not identical to Packrat parsing,
thus the two cannot be used together. Use ``force=True`` to disable any
previous, conflicting settings.
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definición en la línea \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2setuptools_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source_l00985}{985}} del archivo \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2setuptools_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source}{core.\+py}}.

\Hypertarget{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a6d9f91643d37b011b03f417109d4a1aa}\index{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}!enable\_packrat@{enable\_packrat}}
\index{enable\_packrat@{enable\_packrat}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{enable\_packrat()}{enable\_packrat()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a6d9f91643d37b011b03f417109d4a1aa} 
 None setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+enable\+\_\+packrat (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int }]{cache\+\_\+size\+\_\+limit}{ = {\ttfamily 128}, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{bool }]{force}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Enables "packrat" parsing, which adds memoizing to the parsing logic.
Repeated parse attempts at the same string location (which happens
often in many complex grammars) can immediately return a cached value,
instead of re-executing parsing/validating code.  Memoizing is done of
both valid results and parsing exceptions.

Parameters:

- cache_size_limit - (default= ``128``) - if an integer value is provided
  will limit the size of the packrat cache; if None is passed, then
  the cache size will be unbounded; if 0 is passed, the cache will
  be effectively disabled.

This speedup may break existing programs that use parse actions that
have side-effects.  For this reason, packrat parsing is disabled when
you first import pyparsing.  To activate the packrat feature, your
program must call the class method :class:`ParserElement.enable_packrat`.
For best results, call ``enable_packrat()`` immediately after
importing pyparsing.

Example::

    import pyparsing
    pyparsing.ParserElement.enable_packrat()

Packrat parsing works similar but not identical to Bounded Recursion parsing,
thus the two cannot be used together. Use ``force=True`` to disable any
previous, conflicting settings.
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definición en la línea \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2setuptools_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source_l01033}{1033}} del archivo \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2setuptools_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source}{core.\+py}}.

\Hypertarget{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a3d06b11f5c1ed2cf3d0fe9c72303a573}\index{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}!ignore@{ignore}}
\index{ignore@{ignore}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ignore()}{ignore()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a3d06b11f5c1ed2cf3d0fe9c72303a573} 
 "{}Parser\+Element"{} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+ignore (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{"{}Parser\+Element"{}}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Define expression to be ignored (e.g., comments) while doing pattern
matching; may be called repeatedly, to define multiple comment or other
ignorable patterns.

Example::

    patt = Word(alphas)[1, ...]
    patt.parse_string('ablaj /* comment */ lskjd')
    # -> ['ablaj']

    patt.ignore(c_style_comment)
    patt.parse_string('ablaj /* comment */ lskjd')
    # -> ['ablaj', 'lskjd']
\end{DoxyVerb}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_aa60a565d6a1295523b19e7f433d36ce0} 
 "{}Parser\+Element"{} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+ignore\+\_\+whitespace (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{bool }]{recursive}{ = {\ttfamily True}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Enables the skipping of whitespace before matching the characters in the
:class:`ParserElement`'s defined pattern.

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{inline\_literals\_using()}{inline\_literals\_using()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a0357bd15c9ea0e0e4d05592a0dc844bf} 
 None setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+inline\+\_\+literals\+\_\+using (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{type}]{cls}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Set class to be used for inclusion of string literals into a parser.

Example::

    # default literal class used is Literal
    integer = Word(nums)
    date_str = integer("year") + '/' + integer("month") + '/' + integer("day")

    date_str.parse_string("1999/12/31")  # -> ['1999', '/', '12', '/', '31']


    # change to Suppress
    ParserElement.inline_literals_using(Suppress)
    date_str = integer("year") + '/' + integer("month") + '/' + integer("day")

    date_str.parse_string("1999/12/31")  # -> ['1999', '12', '31']
\end{DoxyVerb}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Disables the skipping of whitespace before matching the characters in the

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{matches()}{matches()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a340c5dbbc0054029fa245e398f694e14} 
 bool setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+matches (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{str}]{test\+\_\+string}{, }\item[{bool }]{parse\+\_\+all}{ = {\ttfamily True}, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{bool }]{parse\+All}{ = {\ttfamily True}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Method for quick testing of a parser against a test string. Good for simple
inline microtests of sub expressions while building up larger parser.

Parameters:
- ``test_string`` - to test against this expression for a match
- ``parse_all`` - (default= ``True``) - flag to pass to :class:`parse_string` when running tests

Example::

    expr = Word(nums)
    assert expr.matches("100")
\end{DoxyVerb}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Execute the parse expression on the given file or filename.
If a filename is specified (instead of a file object),
the entire file is opened, read, and closed before parsing.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a4bceb4c6190dd0bd2ea4c6ef9e8fe6f9}\index{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}!parse\_string@{parse\_string}}
\index{parse\_string@{parse\_string}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{parse\_string()}{parse\_string()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a4bceb4c6190dd0bd2ea4c6ef9e8fe6f9} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1results_1_1_parse_results}{Parse\+Results}} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+parse\+\_\+string (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{str}]{instring}{, }\item[{bool }]{parse\+\_\+all}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{bool }]{parse\+All}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Parse a string with respect to the parser definition. This function is intended as the primary interface to the
client code.

:param instring: The input string to be parsed.
:param parse_all: If set, the entire input string must match the grammar.
:param parseAll: retained for pre-PEP8 compatibility, will be removed in a future release.
:raises ParseException: Raised if ``parse_all`` is set and the input string does not match the whole grammar.
:returns: the parsed data as a :class:`ParseResults` object, which may be accessed as a `list`, a `dict`, or
  an object with attributes if the given parser includes results names.

If the input string is required to match the entire grammar, ``parse_all`` flag must be set to ``True``. This
is also equivalent to ending the grammar with :class:`StringEnd`().

To report proper column numbers, ``parse_string`` operates on a copy of the input string where all tabs are
converted to spaces (8 spaces per tab, as per the default in ``string.expandtabs``). If the input string
contains tabs and the grammar uses parse actions that use the ``loc`` argument to index into the string
being parsed, one can ensure a consistent view of the input string by doing one of the following:

- calling ``parse_with_tabs`` on your grammar before calling ``parse_string`` (see :class:`parse_with_tabs`),
- define your parse action using the full ``(s,loc,toks)`` signature, and reference the input string using the
  parse action's ``s`` argument, or
- explicitly expand the tabs in your input string before calling ``parse_string``.

Examples:

By default, partial matches are OK.

>>> res = Word('a').parse_string('aaaaabaaa')
>>> print(res)
['aaaaa']

The parsing behavior varies by the inheriting class of this abstract class. Please refer to the children
directly to see more examples.

It raises an exception if parse_all flag is set and instring does not match the whole grammar.

>>> res = Word('a').parse_string('aaaaabaaa', parse_all=True)
Traceback (most recent call last):
...
pyparsing.ParseException: Expected end of text, found 'b'  (at char 5), (line:1, col:6)
\end{DoxyVerb}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a54fe4317d8405e55796b64a264ac7587} 
 "{}Parser\+Element"{} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+parse\+\_\+with\+\_\+tabs (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Overrides default behavior to expand ``<TAB>`` s to spaces before parsing the input string.
Must be called before ``parse_string`` when the input grammar contains elements that
match ``<TAB>`` characters.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a67d4875fb1c02837aae5bb1e763532ba}\index{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}!run\_tests@{run\_tests}}
\index{run\_tests@{run\_tests}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{run\_tests()}{run\_tests()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a67d4875fb1c02837aae5bb1e763532ba} 
 Tuple\mbox{[}bool, List\mbox{[}Tuple\mbox{[}str, Union\mbox{[}\mbox{\hyperlink{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1results_1_1_parse_results}{Parse\+Results}}, Exception\mbox{]}\mbox{]}\mbox{]}\mbox{]} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+run\+\_\+tests (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{Union\mbox{[}str, List\mbox{[}str\mbox{]}\mbox{]}}]{tests}{, }\item[{bool }]{parse\+\_\+all}{ = {\ttfamily True}, }\item[{typing.\+Optional\mbox{[}Union\mbox{[}"{}Parser\+Element"{}, str\mbox{]}\mbox{]} }]{comment}{ = {\ttfamily "{}\#"{}}, }\item[{bool }]{full\+\_\+dump}{ = {\ttfamily True}, }\item[{bool }]{print\+\_\+results}{ = {\ttfamily True}, }\item[{bool }]{failure\+\_\+tests}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{Callable\mbox{[}\mbox{[}str, \mbox{\hyperlink{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1results_1_1_parse_results}{Parse\+Results}}\mbox{]}, str\mbox{]} }]{post\+\_\+parse}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{typing.\+Optional\mbox{[}Text\+IO\mbox{]} }]{file}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{bool }]{with\+\_\+line\+\_\+numbers}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{bool }]{parse\+All}{ = {\ttfamily True}, }\item[{bool }]{full\+Dump}{ = {\ttfamily True}, }\item[{bool }]{print\+Results}{ = {\ttfamily True}, }\item[{bool }]{failure\+Tests}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{Callable\mbox{[}\mbox{[}str, \mbox{\hyperlink{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1results_1_1_parse_results}{Parse\+Results}}\mbox{]}, str\mbox{]} }]{post\+Parse}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Execute the parse expression on a series of test strings, showing each
test, the parsed results or where the parse failed. Quick and easy way to
run a parse expression against a list of sample strings.

Parameters:
- ``tests`` - a list of separate test strings, or a multiline string of test strings
- ``parse_all`` - (default= ``True``) - flag to pass to :class:`parse_string` when running tests
- ``comment`` - (default= ``'#'``) - expression for indicating embedded comments in the test
  string; pass None to disable comment filtering
- ``full_dump`` - (default= ``True``) - dump results as list followed by results names in nested outline;
  if False, only dump nested list
- ``print_results`` - (default= ``True``) prints test output to stdout
- ``failure_tests`` - (default= ``False``) indicates if these tests are expected to fail parsing
- ``post_parse`` - (default= ``None``) optional callback for successful parse results; called as
  `fn(test_string, parse_results)` and returns a string to be added to the test output
- ``file`` - (default= ``None``) optional file-like object to which test output will be written;
  if None, will default to ``sys.stdout``
- ``with_line_numbers`` - default= ``False``) show test strings with line and column numbers

Returns: a (success, results) tuple, where success indicates that all tests succeeded
(or failed if ``failure_tests`` is True), and the results contain a list of lines of each
test's output

Example::

    number_expr = pyparsing_common.number.copy()

    result = number_expr.run_tests('''
        # unsigned integer
        100
        # negative integer
        -100
        # float with scientific notation
        6.02e23
        # integer with scientific notation
        1e-12
        ''')
    print("Success" if result[0] else "Failed!")

    result = number_expr.run_tests('''
        # stray character
        100Z
        # missing leading digit before '.'
        -.100
        # too many '.'
        3.14.159
        ''', failure_tests=True)
    print("Success" if result[0] else "Failed!")

prints::

    # unsigned integer
    100
    [100]

    # negative integer
    -100
    [-100]

    # float with scientific notation
    6.02e23
    [6.02e+23]

    # integer with scientific notation
    1e-12
    [1e-12]

    Success

    # stray character
    100Z
       ^
    FAIL: Expected end of text (at char 3), (line:1, col:4)

    # missing leading digit before '.'
    -.100
    ^
    FAIL: Expected {real number with scientific notation | real number | signed integer} (at char 0), (line:1, col:1)

    # too many '.'
    3.14.159
        ^
    FAIL: Expected end of text (at char 4), (line:1, col:5)

    Success

Each test string must be on a single line. If you want to test a string that spans multiple
lines, create a test like this::

    expr.run_tests(r"this is a test\\n of strings that spans \\n 3 lines")

(Note that this is a raw string literal, you must include the leading ``'r'``.)
\end{DoxyVerb}

\index{scan\_string@{scan\_string}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{scan\_string()}{scan\_string()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a1e2aa4fc1e0debef9f876b7e1ccbfb62} 
 Generator\mbox{[}Tuple\mbox{[}\mbox{\hyperlink{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1results_1_1_parse_results}{Parse\+Results}}, int, int\mbox{]}, None, None\mbox{]} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+scan\+\_\+string (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{str}]{instring}{, }\item[{int }]{max\+\_\+matches}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacesetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_a63067d52959e8290c5b080ac60ea60d8}{\+\_\+\+MAX\+\_\+\+INT}}}, }\item[{bool }]{overlap}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{bool }]{debug}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{int }]{max\+Matches}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacesetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_a63067d52959e8290c5b080ac60ea60d8}{\+\_\+\+MAX\+\_\+\+INT}}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Scan the input string for expression matches.  Each match will return the
matching tokens, start location, and end location.  May be called with optional
``max_matches`` argument, to clip scanning after 'n' matches are found.  If
``overlap`` is specified, then overlapping matches will be reported.

Note that the start and end locations are reported relative to the string
being parsed.  See :class:`parse_string` for more information on parsing
strings with embedded tabs.

Example::

    source = "sldjf123lsdjjkf345sldkjf879lkjsfd987"
    print(source)
    for tokens, start, end in Word(alphas).scan_string(source):
        print(' '*start + '^'*(end-start))
        print(' '*start + tokens[0])

prints::

    sldjf123lsdjjkf345sldkjf879lkjsfd987
    ^^^^^
    sldjf
            ^^^^^^^
            lsdjjkf
                      ^^^^^^
                      sldkjf
                               ^^^^^^
                               lkjsfd
\end{DoxyVerb}

\index{search\_string@{search\_string}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{search\_string()}{search\_string()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_afd39623fe4bffcc694a482c83b93fd06} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1results_1_1_parse_results}{Parse\+Results}} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+search\+\_\+string (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{str}]{instring}{, }\item[{int }]{max\+\_\+matches}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacesetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_a63067d52959e8290c5b080ac60ea60d8}{\+\_\+\+MAX\+\_\+\+INT}}}, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{bool }]{debug}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{int }]{max\+Matches}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacesetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_a63067d52959e8290c5b080ac60ea60d8}{\+\_\+\+MAX\+\_\+\+INT}}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Another extension to :class:`scan_string`, simplifying the access to the tokens found
to match the given parse expression.  May be called with optional
``max_matches`` argument, to clip searching after 'n' matches are found.

Example::

    # a capitalized word starts with an uppercase letter, followed by zero or more lowercase letters
    cap_word = Word(alphas.upper(), alphas.lower())

    print(cap_word.search_string("More than Iron, more than Lead, more than Gold I need Electricity"))

    # the sum() builtin can be used to merge results into a single ParseResults object
    print(sum(cap_word.search_string("More than Iron, more than Lead, more than Gold I need Electricity")))

prints::

    [['More'], ['Iron'], ['Lead'], ['Gold'], ['I'], ['Electricity']]
    ['More', 'Iron', 'Lead', 'Gold', 'I', 'Electricity']
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a590fbf8b1488f90c43778e6f11b56391}\index{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}!set\_debug@{set\_debug}}
\index{set\_debug@{set\_debug}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{set\_debug()}{set\_debug()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a590fbf8b1488f90c43778e6f11b56391} 
 "{}Parser\+Element"{} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+set\+\_\+debug (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{bool }]{flag}{ = {\ttfamily True}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Enable display of debugging messages while doing pattern matching.
Set ``flag`` to ``True`` to enable, ``False`` to disable.

Example::

    wd = Word(alphas).set_name("alphaword")
    integer = Word(nums).set_name("numword")
    term = wd | integer

    # turn on debugging for wd
    wd.set_debug()

    term[1, ...].parse_string("abc 123 xyz 890")

prints::

    Match alphaword at loc 0(1,1)
    Matched alphaword -> ['abc']
    Match alphaword at loc 3(1,4)
    Exception raised:Expected alphaword (at char 4), (line:1, col:5)
    Match alphaword at loc 7(1,8)
    Matched alphaword -> ['xyz']
    Match alphaword at loc 11(1,12)
    Exception raised:Expected alphaword (at char 12), (line:1, col:13)
    Match alphaword at loc 15(1,16)
    Exception raised:Expected alphaword (at char 15), (line:1, col:16)

The output shown is that produced by the default debug actions - custom debug actions can be
specified using :class:`set_debug_actions`. Prior to attempting
to match the ``wd`` expression, the debugging message ``"Match <exprname> at loc <n>(<line>,<col>)"``
is shown. Then if the parse succeeds, a ``"Matched"`` message is shown, or an ``"Exception raised"``
message is shown. Also note the use of :class:`set_name` to assign a human-readable name to the expression,
which makes debugging and exception messages easier to understand - for instance, the default
name created for the :class:`Word` expression without calling ``set_name`` is ``"W:(A-Za-z)"``.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Customize display of debugging messages while doing pattern matching:

- ``start_action`` - method to be called when an expression is about to be parsed;
  should have the signature ``fn(input_string: str, location: int, expression: ParserElement, cache_hit: bool)``

- ``success_action`` - method to be called when an expression has successfully parsed;
  should have the signature ``fn(input_string: str, start_location: int, end_location: int, expression: ParserELement, parsed_tokens: ParseResults, cache_hit: bool)``

- ``exception_action`` - method to be called when expression fails to parse;
  should have the signature ``fn(input_string: str, location: int, expression: ParserElement, exception: Exception, cache_hit: bool)``
\end{DoxyVerb}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Overrides the default whitespace chars

Example::

    # default whitespace chars are space, <TAB> and newline
    Word(alphas)[1, ...].parse_string("abc def\nghi jkl")  # -> ['abc', 'def', 'ghi', 'jkl']

    # change to just treat newline as significant
    ParserElement.set_default_whitespace_chars(" \t")
    Word(alphas)[1, ...].parse_string("abc def\nghi jkl")  # -> ['abc', 'def']
\end{DoxyVerb}

if it is desired to stop parsing immediately.\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a62ede4c29e13067f196ea53617979181}\index{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}!set\_parse\_action@{set\_parse\_action}}
\index{set\_parse\_action@{set\_parse\_action}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{set\_parse\_action()}{set\_parse\_action()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a62ede4c29e13067f196ea53617979181} 
 "{}Parser\+Element"{} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+set\+\_\+parse\+\_\+action (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacesetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_a516abf6fa2aa5dd9b5a8e4c4a76fc8d2}{Parse\+Action}}}]{fns}{, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{kwargs}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Define one or more actions to perform when successfully matching parse element definition.

Parse actions can be called to perform data conversions, do extra validation,
update external data structures, or enhance or replace the parsed tokens.
Each parse action ``fn`` is a callable method with 0-3 arguments, called as
``fn(s, loc, toks)`` , ``fn(loc, toks)`` , ``fn(toks)`` , or just ``fn()`` , where:

- s   = the original string being parsed (see note below)
- loc = the location of the matching substring
- toks = a list of the matched tokens, packaged as a :class:`ParseResults` object

The parsed tokens are passed to the parse action as ParseResults. They can be
modified in place using list-style append, extend, and pop operations to update
the parsed list elements; and with dictionary-style item set and del operations
to add, update, or remove any named results. If the tokens are modified in place,
it is not necessary to return them with a return statement.

Parse actions can also completely replace the given tokens, with another ``ParseResults``
object, or with some entirely different object (common for parse actions that perform data
conversions). A convenient way to build a new parse result is to define the values
using a dict, and then create the return value using :class:`ParseResults.from_dict`.

If None is passed as the ``fn`` parse action, all previously added parse actions for this
expression are cleared.

Optional keyword arguments:

- call_during_try = (default= ``False``) indicate if parse action should be run during
  lookaheads and alternate testing. For parse actions that have side effects, it is
  important to only call the parse action once it is determined that it is being
  called as part of a successful parse. For parse actions that perform additional
  validation, then call_during_try should be passed as True, so that the validation
  code is included in the preliminary "try" parses.

Note: the default parsing behavior is to expand tabs in the input string
before starting the parsing process.  See :class:`parse_string` for more
information on parsing strings containing ``<TAB>`` s, and suggested
methods to maintain a consistent view of the parsed string, the parse
location, and line and column positions within the parsed string.

Example::

    # parse dates in the form YYYY/MM/DD

    # use parse action to convert toks from str to int at parse time
    def convert_to_int(toks):
        return int(toks[0])

    # use a parse action to verify that the date is a valid date
    def is_valid_date(instring, loc, toks):
        from datetime import date
        year, month, day = toks[::2]
        try:
            date(year, month, day)
        except ValueError:
            raise ParseException(instring, loc, "invalid date given")

    integer = Word(nums)
    date_str = integer + '/' + integer + '/' + integer

    # add parse actions
    integer.set_parse_action(convert_to_int)
    date_str.set_parse_action(is_valid_date)

    # note that integer fields are now ints, not strings
    date_str.run_tests('''
        # successful parse - note that integer fields were converted to ints
        1999/12/31

        # fail - invalid date
        1999/13/31
        ''')
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definición en la línea \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2setuptools_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source_l00595}{595}} del archivo \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2setuptools_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source}{core.\+py}}.



Hace referencia a \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2setuptools_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source_l00262}{setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+\_\+trim\+\_\+arity()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2pip_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source_l00486}{pip.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+call\+During\+Try}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2pkg__resources_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source_l00480}{pkg\+\_\+resources.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+call\+During\+Try}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2setuptools_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source_l00480}{call\+During\+Try}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2pip_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source_l00462}{pip.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+parse\+Action}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2pkg__resources_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source_l00456}{pkg\+\_\+resources.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+parse\+Action}} y \mbox{\hyperlink{microservicio__data__stream_2venv_2_lib_2site-packages_2setuptools_2__vendor_2pyparsing_2core_8py_source_l00456}{parse\+Action}}.

\Hypertarget{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_aa174c848de2d5095272991c738286d92}\index{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}!set\_results\_name@{set\_results\_name}}
\index{set\_results\_name@{set\_results\_name}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{set\_results\_name()}{set\_results\_name()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_aa174c848de2d5095272991c738286d92} 
 "{}Parser\+Element"{} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+set\+\_\+results\+\_\+name (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{str}]{name}{, }\item[{bool }]{list\+\_\+all\+\_\+matches}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{bool }]{list\+All\+Matches}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Define name for referencing matching tokens as a nested attribute
of the returned parse results.

Normally, results names are assigned as you would assign keys in a dict:
any existing value is overwritten by later values. If it is necessary to
keep all values captured for a particular results name, call ``set_results_name``
with ``list_all_matches`` = True.

NOTE: ``set_results_name`` returns a *copy* of the original :class:`ParserElement` object;
this is so that the client can define a basic element, such as an
integer, and reference it in multiple places with different names.

You can also set results names using the abbreviated syntax,
``expr("name")`` in place of ``expr.set_results_name("name")``
- see :class:`__call__`. If ``list_all_matches`` is required, use
``expr("name*")``.

Example::

    date_str = (integer.set_results_name("year") + '/'
                + integer.set_results_name("month") + '/'
                + integer.set_results_name("day"))

    # equivalent form:
    date_str = integer("year") + '/' + integer("month") + '/' + integer("day")
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a851b91f91735a7984ff943924b8f5e53}\index{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}!split@{split}}
\index{split@{split}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{split()}{split()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a851b91f91735a7984ff943924b8f5e53} 
 Generator\mbox{[}str, None, None\mbox{]} setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+split (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{str}]{instring}{, }\item[{int }]{maxsplit}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacesetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_a63067d52959e8290c5b080ac60ea60d8}{\+\_\+\+MAX\+\_\+\+INT}}}, }\item[{bool }]{include\+\_\+separators}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{}]{include\+Separators}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Generator method to split a string using the given expression as a separator.
May be called with optional ``maxsplit`` argument, to limit the number of splits;
and the optional ``include_separators`` argument (default= ``False``), if the separating
matching text should be included in the split results.

Example::

    punc = one_of(list(".,;:/-!?"))
    print(list(punc.split("This, this?, this sentence, is badly punctuated!")))

prints::

    ['This', ' this', '', ' this sentence', ' is badly punctuated', '']
\end{DoxyVerb}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Suppress warnings emitted for a particular diagnostic on this expression.

    base = pp.Forward()
    base.suppress_warning(Diagnostics.warn_on_parse_using_empty_Forward)

    print(base.parseString("x"))
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a23d5d123f33508735ec8eefe96840071}\index{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}!transform\_string@{transform\_string}}
\index{transform\_string@{transform\_string}!setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement@{setuptools.\_vendor.pyparsing.core.ParserElement}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{transform\_string()}{transform\_string()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classsetuptools_1_1__vendor_1_1pyparsing_1_1core_1_1_parser_element_a23d5d123f33508735ec8eefe96840071} 
 str setuptools.\+\_\+vendor.\+pyparsing.\+core.\+Parser\+Element.\+transform\+\_\+string (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{str}]{instring}{, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{bool }]{debug}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Extension to :class:`scan_string`, to modify matching text with modified tokens that may
be returned from a parse action.  To use ``transform_string``, define a grammar and
attach a parse action to it that modifies the returned token list.
Invoking ``transform_string()`` on a target string will then scan for matches,
and replace the matched text patterns according to the logic in the parse
action.  ``transform_string()`` returns the resulting transformed string.

Example::

    wd = Word(alphas)
    wd.set_parse_action(lambda toks: toks[0].title())

    print(wd.transform_string("now is the winter of our discontent made glorious summer by this sun of york."))

prints::

    Now Is The Winter Of Our Discontent Made Glorious Summer By This Sun Of York.
\end{DoxyVerb}
